# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Leader Election Patterns Across K8s Ecosystem

## Your Task

Compare leader election implementations across kubernetes/kubernetes and etcd-io/etcd. Find Go source files in each repo that implement leader election: the lease-based election in k8s, the Raft-based leader in etcd, and how each handles leader failover and re-election.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:

64-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of leader election implementations across the two repositories. Here's what I found:

## Summary

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with a detailed comparison of leader election patterns between Kubernetes and etcd:

### **Kubernetes Implementation (Lease-Based)**
- Uses **distributed leases** via Kubernetes Lease API objects as coordination mechanism
- Time-based polling with configurable durations (LeaseDuration, RenewDeadline, RetryPeriod)
- Fast path for leader renewal (optimistic update) and slow path (fetch-then-update)
- Failover triggered by lease expiration, detected by polling
- Supports coordinated leader election with multiple candidates negotiating succession

### **etcd Implementation (Raft-Based)**  
- Uses **Raft consensus algorithm** for leader election at cluster level
- Heartbeat timeout-based detection (ElectionTimeout = ElectionTicks × TickMs)
- Pre-Vote optimization to reduce disruptive elections
- Client-facing election API: Campaign, Proclaim, Resign, Leader, Observe
- Deterministic quorum-based election with strong consistency guarantees

### **Key Files Identified**
- **Kubernetes**: LeaderElector, LeaseLock, resourcelock interface, healthz adaptor, lease candidate
- **etcd**: Raft state machine, election gRPC service, transport layer, configuration

The answer includes 14 key files, 25+ important symbols (types and functions), and a detailed execution chain showing how each system orchestrates leader election and handles failover scenarios.

\"symbol\": \"ensureLeadership\"}\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"## Leader Election Pattern Comparison: Kubernetes vs etcd\\n\\n### Kubernetes: Lease-Based Leader Election\\n\\nKubernetes implements a **distributed lease-based leader election** mechanism through its client-go library, primarily used by control plane components like the scheduler and controller-manager.\\n\\n**Core Architecture:**\\n- **Resource Lock Interface** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/interface.go): Defines the abstraction for leader election resources supporting Get, Create, and Update operations\\n- **LeaseLock Implementation** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/resourcelock/leaselock.go): Uses Kubernetes Lease API objects (v1.coordination.k8s.io) to store election state with fields: HolderIdentity, LeaseDurationSeconds, AcquireTime, RenewTime, LeaderTransitions\\n- **LeaderElector** (staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go): Main client managing the election lifecycle with configurable timers (LeaseDuration, RenewDeadline, RetryPeriod)\\n\\n**Election Algorithm:**\\n1. **Acquisition Phase (acquire method)**: Calls tryAcquireOrRenew repeatedly with jitter-based backoff until successful\\n2. **Fast Path Renewal**: If already leading and lease is valid, optimistically renews the lease\\n3. **Slow Path Renewal**: Fetches current lease record, checks expiration (LeaseDurationSeconds), and updates if still valid\\n4. **Lease Expiration Detection**: Uses local observedTime + LeaseDurationSeconds to detect lease timeout\\n5. **Release/Failover**: On context cancellation or renewal failure, calls release() to set LeaseDurationSeconds=1 for quick re-election\\n\\n**Failover Mechanism:**\\n- Non-leader candidates continuously poll the lease resource (RetryPeriod intervals)\\n- When a lease expires (no renewal within LeaseDurationSeconds), candidates can immediately acquire it\\n- LeaderTransitions counter tracks leadership changes for monitoring\\n- Health check integration via HealthzAdaptor enables graceful shutdown notification\\n- Coordinated Leader Election (optional, v1beta1) allows multiple candidates to negotiate succession\\n\\n**Key Design Principles:**\\n- Clock-skew tolerant (configurable LeaseDuration vs RenewDeadline ratio)\\n- No external consensus required - uses Kubernetes API as storage\\n- Supports timeout-based and event-driven detection\\n- Records holder identity, acquisition time, and renewal time\\n\\n### etcd: Raft-Based Leader Election\\n\\netcd implements leader election through **Raft consensus** at two levels: the core cluster membership protocol and a client-facing election API.\\n\\n**Raft Consensus Layer** (Embedded in etcd):\\n- **raftNode** (server/etcdserver/raft.go): Manages the Raft state machine with election timeout based on ElectionTicks\\n- **Raft States**: Follower, Candidate, Leader (managed by go.etcd.io/raft/v3 library)\\n- **Leader Election Trigger**: Election occurs when no heartbeat received within ElectionTimeout (ElectionTicks \u00d7 TickMs milliseconds)\\n- **Pre-Vote Optimization** (server/config/config.go): Reduces disruptive elections when nodes rejoin; candidates first ask for votes without updating term\\n- **Initial Election Tick Advance**: Fast-forwards election ticks on startup to accelerate initial leader election (configurable via --initial-election-tick-advance flag)\\n\\n**Election Timeout Calculation** (server/config/config.go):\\n- ElectionTimeout = ElectionTicks \u00d7 TickMs (default: 10 ticks \u00d7 100ms = 1 second)\\n- Automatic adjustment on server restart to prevent disruptive re-elections\\n\\n**Client-Facing Election API** (server/etcdserver/api/v3election/):\\n- **Campaign**: Place a candidate in the election, wait for previous leader's deletion via watchDeletes()\\n- **Proclaim**: Leader updates its value in the election using transactional compare-and-set with CreateRevision check\\n- **Resign**: Leader voluntarily steps down by deleting its key\\n- **Leader**: Query current election leader by getting first key with WithFirstCreate ordering\\n- **Observe**: Stream ordered leader proclamations as they occur\\n\\nThe gRPC service (v3election.proto) wraps concurrency.Election client through server-side session management.\\n\\n**Failover Mechanism:**\\n1. **Leader Failure Detection**: Followers detect leader absence when heartbeat messages stop arriving\\n2. **Timeout-Triggered Election**: After ElectionTimeout, followers become candidates and request votes\\n3. **Consensus-Based Selection**: Only candidates with majority votes become leaders (Raft guarantees)\\n4. **Automatic Log Replication**: New leader pulls missing log entries from followers before committing\\n5. **ensureLeadership()** (server/etcdserver/server.go): Verifies leadership via linearizable read; checks raftStatus().Lead equals local MemberID\\n6. **Leadership Transfer**: Graceful handoff when leader steps down\\n\\n**Raft Message Transport** (server/etcdserver/api/rafthttp/transport.go):\\n- HTTP/2 based peer-to-peer transport for Raft messages\\n- LeaderStats tracks replication progress to followers\\n- Separate optimized stream for heartbeat AppendEntries messages from leaders\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | etcd |\\n|--------|-----------|------|\\n| **Mechanism** | Distributed lease with API-based storage | Raft consensus algorithm |\\n| **Storage** | Kubernetes Lease objects (etcd or external) | In-memory Raft log + persistent WAL |\\n| **Leader Detection** | Polling-based (RetryPeriod) | Heartbeat timeouts (ElectionTicks) |\\n| **Failover Time** | Configurable (LeaseDuration, default 15s) | Bounded by ElectionTimeout (default 1s) |\\n| **Consistency** | Eventual consistency via API | Strong consistency via Raft quorum |\\n| **Scalability** | Limited by API server throughput | Peer-to-peer consensus independent of API |\\n| **Election Coordination** | Sequential leasing with renewal | Parallel voting with quorum requirement |\\n| **Monitoring** | Via LeaderElectionRecord metadata | Via Raft metrics and LeaderStats |\\n\\n### Election State Tracking\\n\\n**Kubernetes LeaderElectionRecord** fields:\\n- HolderIdentity: Current leader ID\\n- AcquireTime: When leadership was acquired\\n- RenewTime: Last renewal timestamp\\n- LeaseDurationSeconds: Lease validity period\\n- LeaderTransitions: Count of leadership changes\\n- PreferredHolder: Next leader candidate (coordinated election)\\n- Strategy: Election strategy being used\\n\\n**etcd Raft Election** state:\\n- raftStatus.Lead: Current leader node ID\\n- raftStatus.Term: Current election term\\n- raftStatus.State: Node's state (Follower/Candidate/Leader)\\n- Raft log: Command sequence establishing consensus\\n- Lease ID: Associated session lease for key holding\\n\\n### Failover and Re-Election Triggers\\n\\n**Kubernetes Triggers:**\\n1. Lease.RenewTime + LeaseDurationSeconds < current time\\n2. Explicit release (ReleaseOnCancel=true on context cancel)\\n3. Failed Update operations\\n4. LeaderTransitions threshold (coordinated election mode)\\n\\n**etcd Triggers:**\\n1. No heartbeat messages within ElectionTimeout\\n2. Leadership transfer request (Leader.TransferLeadership)\\n3. Configuration changes (membership changes trigger re-election)\\n4. Explicit resignation via Election.Resign() API\\n\\nBoth systems ensure safe, deterministic leadership transitions through either time-based leasing (k8s) or consensus voting (etcd), with proper handling of network partitions and cascading failures.\"\n}\n",
